Question 1easy

Which of the following elements is a non-metal and exists as a diatomic molecule at room temperature?

  1. Oxygen
  2. Sodium
  3. Iron
  4. Helium
Show answer

Answer: Oxygen

Oxygen is a non-metal and exists as O₂ (a diatomic molecule) at room temperature. The other options are either metals or noble gases.

Question 2easy

A solution turns red litmus paper blue. This solution is likely to be:

  1. Acidic
  2. Basic
  3. Neutral
  4. Amphoteric
Show answer

Answer: Basic

Red litmus paper turning blue indicates a basic solution. Acids turn blue litmus red, and neutral solutions do not change the color of litmus.

Question 3medium

Which of the following elements has the highest electronegativity?

  1. Fluorine
  2. Chlorine
  3. Oxygen
  4. Nitrogen
Show answer

Answer: Fluorine

Electronegativity generally increases across a period and decreases down a group. Fluorine is in the top right of the periodic table (excluding noble gases).

Question 4medium

An aqueous solution turns red litmus paper blue. What is the probable pH range of this solution?

  1. pH < 7
  2. pH = 7
  3. pH > 7
  4. pH = 0
Show answer

Answer: pH > 7

Red litmus paper turning blue indicates a basic solution. Basic solutions have a pH greater than 7.

Question 5medium

Which type of chemical reaction is represented by the equation: CaCO₃(s) → CaO(s) + CO₂(g)?

  1. Combination reaction
  2. Decomposition reaction
  3. Displacement reaction
  4. Double displacement reaction
Show answer

Answer: Decomposition reaction

In a decomposition reaction, a single compound breaks down into two or more simpler substances. Here, calcium carbonate breaks into calcium oxide and carbon dioxide.

Question 6medium

Which of the following metals is most reactive?

  1. Copper
  2. Iron
  3. Sodium
  4. Silver
Show answer

Answer: Sodium

Reactivity of metals generally increases as you go down a group and decreases across a period. Sodium is an alkali metal and highly reactive.

Question 7medium

What is the chemical formula for washing soda?

  1. NaOH
  2. Na₂CO₃
  3. NaHCO₃
  4. CaCO₃
Show answer

Answer: Na₂CO₃

Washing soda is chemically known as sodium carbonate (Na₂CO₃). Sodium bicarbonate (NaHCO₃) is baking soda.

Question 8hard

A student performs three experiments. In Experiment 1, a solution turns red litmus blue. In Experiment 2, a different solution reacts with zinc metal to produce hydrogen gas. In Experiment 3, a third solution reacts with sodium carbonate to release carbon dioxide gas. If the solution from Experiment 1 is then mixed with the solution from Experiment 3, what is the most likely observation and its chemical nature?

  1. No visible change, as both are neutral solutions.
  2. A vigorous exothermic reaction, indicating neutralization.
  3. Formation of a precipitate, suggesting a double displacement reaction.
  4. Release of a pungent gas, characteristic of an oxidation-reduction reaction.
Show answer

Answer: A vigorous exothermic reaction, indicating neutralization.

Experiment 1 indicates a base, and Experiment 3 indicates an acid. Mixing an acid and a base results in a neutralization reaction, which is typically exothermic.

Question 9hard

Consider the elements X, Y, and Z. Element X forms a stable ionic compound with chlorine, where X has a +2 charge. Element Y is a non-metal that exists as a diatomic gas at room temperature and is highly reactive. Element Z is a metalloid that can act as both an acid and a base. Which of the following statements is most accurate regarding their positions in the periodic table and their chemical properties?

  1. X is likely in Group 1, Y in Group 17, and Z in Group 13; X is more reactive than Z.
  2. X is likely in Group 2, Y in Group 17, and Z in Group 13; X has a lower ionization energy than Z.
  3. X is likely in Group 13, Y in Group 16, and Z in Group 14; Z exhibits metallic character.
  4. X is likely in Group 2, Y in Group 16, and Z in Group 15; Y forms acidic oxides.
Show answer

Answer: X is likely in Group 2, Y in Group 17, and Z in Group 13; X has a lower ionization energy than Z.

X (+2 charge) suggests Group 2. Y (diatomic, highly reactive non-metal) suggests Group 17 (halogens). Z (metalloid, amphoteric) suggests Group 13 (e.g., Boron, Aluminum). Group 2 metals have lower ionization energies than metalloids in Group 13.

Question 10hard

A student has three unlabeled bottles, each containing a colorless liquid: dilute hydrochloric acid, dilute sodium hydroxide, and distilled water. The student has access to red litmus paper, blue litmus paper, and phenolphthalein indicator. Which is the most efficient sequence of tests to correctly identify all three liquids?

  1. Test each liquid with red litmus paper, then with blue litmus paper.
  2. Add phenolphthalein to each liquid; then use litmus paper if no color change occurs.
  3. Test each liquid with blue litmus paper. For those that show no change, add red litmus paper. If still no change, use phenolphthalein.
  4. Test each liquid with red litmus paper. For those that show no change, add phenolphthalein. For the remaining, use blue litmus paper.
Show answer

Answer: Test each liquid with red litmus paper. For those that show no change, add phenolphthalein. For the remaining, use blue litmus paper.

Red litmus identifies acid (turns blue). Phenolphthalein identifies base (turns pink). The remaining colorless liquid is distilled water.

  1. Basic
  2. Acidic

Answer: Neutral

A neutral solution does not change the color of either red or blue litmus paper. Therefore, the solution is neutral.

  2. Turns blue

Question 17medium

Which type of chemical reaction is represented by the equation: 2KClO₃(s) → 2KCl(s) + 3O₂(g)?

  1. Decomposition reaction
  2. Synthesis reaction
  3. Single displacement reaction
  4. Double displacement reaction
Show answer

Answer: Decomposition reaction

A single compound breaks down into two or more simpler substances. This is the definition of a decomposition reaction.

Question 18medium

Which type of chemical reaction is represented by the equation: 2Mg(s) + O₂(g) → 2MgO(s)?

  1. Combustion reaction
  2. Decomposition reaction
  3. Synthesis reaction
  4. Single displacement reaction
Show answer

Answer: Synthesis reaction

Two or more reactants combine to form a single, more complex product. This is the definition of a synthesis reaction.

Question 19medium

Which type of chemical reaction is represented by the equation: Zn(s) + CuSO₄(aq) → ZnSO₄(aq) + Cu(s)?

  1. Decomposition reaction
  2. Synthesis reaction
  3. Single displacement reaction
  4. Double displacement reaction
Show answer

Answer: Single displacement reaction

One element replaces another element in a compound. This describes a single displacement reaction.

Question 22hard

A student performs two experiments. In Experiment 1, a solution turns red litmus blue. In Experiment 2, a different solution reacts with magnesium metal to produce hydrogen gas. If the solution from Experiment 1 is then mixed with the solution from Experiment 2, what is the most likely observation and its chemical nature?

  1. The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.
  2. The solution changes color, indicating a redox reaction.
  3. Gas bubbles are produced, indicating a decomposition reaction.
  4. A precipitate forms, indicating a double displacement reaction.
Show answer

Answer: The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.

Experiment 1 indicates a base, Experiment 2 indicates an acid. Mixing an acid and a base results in a neutralization reaction, which is typically exothermic.

Question 23hard

A student performs four experiments. In Experiment A, a solution turns blue litmus red. In Experiment B, a different solution reacts with calcium metal to produce hydrogen gas. In Experiment C, a third solution reacts with sodium bicarbonate to release carbon dioxide gas. In Experiment D, a fourth solution turns red litmus blue. If the solution from Experiment A is then mixed with the solution from Experiment D, what is the most likely observation and its chemical nature?

  1. The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.
  2. The solution changes color, indicating a complexation reaction.
  3. Gas bubbles are produced, indicating a gas evolution reaction.
  4. A precipitate forms, indicating a precipitation reaction.
Show answer

Answer: The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.

Experiment A indicates an acid, Experiment D indicates a base. Mixing an acid and a base results in a neutralization reaction, which is typically exothermic.

Question 24hard

A student performs five experiments. In Experiment I, a solution turns red litmus blue. In Experiment II, a different solution reacts with potassium metal to produce hydrogen gas. In Experiment III, a third solution reacts with potassium carbonate to release carbon dioxide gas. In Experiment IV, a fourth solution turns blue litmus red. In Experiment V, a fifth solution is neutral. If the solution from Experiment I is then mixed with the solution from Experiment IV, what is the most likely observation and its chemical nature?

  1. The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.
  2. The solution remains unchanged, indicating no reaction.
  3. A solid forms, indicating a precipitation reaction.
  4. The solution cools down, indicating an endothermic reaction.
Show answer

Answer: The solution becomes warmer, indicating an exothermic neutralization reaction.

Experiment I indicates a base, Experiment IV indicates an acid. Mixing an acid and a base results in a neutralization reaction, which is typically exothermic.

Question 25hard

Consider the elements X, Y, and Z. Element X forms a stable ionic compound with chlorine, where X has a +1 charge. Element Y is a non-metal that exists as a diatomic gas at room temperature and is highly reactive. Element Z is a metalloid that can act as both an acid and a base. Which of the following statements is most accurate regarding their positions in the periodic table and their chemical properties?

  1. X is likely an alkali metal, Y is likely a halogen, and Z is likely in Group 14 or 15.
  2. X is likely an alkaline earth metal, Y is likely oxygen, and Z is likely boron.
  3. X is likely a transition metal, Y is likely nitrogen, and Z is likely silicon.
  4. X is likely a noble gas, Y is likely hydrogen, and Z is likely germanium.
Show answer

Answer: X is likely an alkali metal, Y is likely a halogen, and Z is likely in Group 14 or 15.

X with a +1 charge suggests Group 1. Y as a reactive diatomic non-metal suggests halogens (Group 17). Z as an amphoteric metalloid points to elements like Si, Ge, As, Sb (Groups 14, 15).

Question 26hard

Consider the elements X, Y, and Z. Element X forms a stable ionic compound with chlorine, where X has a +3 charge. Element Y is a non-metal that exists as a diatomic gas at room temperature and is highly unreactive. Element Z is a metalloid that can act as both an acid and a base. Which of the following statements is most accurate regarding their positions in the periodic table and their chemical properties?

  1. X is likely a Group 13 metal, Y is likely nitrogen, and Z is likely in Group 14 or 15.
  2. X is likely an alkaline earth metal, Y is likely oxygen, and Z is likely boron.
  3. X is likely an alkali metal, Y is likely a halogen, and Z is likely silicon.
  4. X is likely a transition metal, Y is likely hydrogen, and Z is likely germanium.
Show answer

Answer: X is likely a Group 13 metal, Y is likely nitrogen, and Z is likely in Group 14 or 15.

X with a +3 charge suggests Group 13. Y as an unreactive diatomic non-metal is nitrogen. Z as an amphoteric metalloid points to elements like Si, Ge, As, Sb (Groups 14, 15).

Question 27hard

A student has three unlabeled bottles, each containing a colorless liquid: dilute sulfuric acid, dilute potassium hydroxide, and distilled water. The student has access to red litmus paper, blue litmus paper, and phenolphthalein indicator. Which is the most efficient sequence of tests to correctly identify all three liquids?

  1. Test with phenolphthalein, then use red litmus paper on the remaining liquids.
  2. Test with blue litmus paper, then use red litmus paper on the remaining liquids.
  3. Test with red litmus paper, then use blue litmus paper on the remaining liquids.
  4. Test with phenolphthalein, then use blue litmus paper on the remaining liquids.
Show answer

Answer: Test with phenolphthalein, then use red litmus paper on the remaining liquids.

Phenolphthalein identifies the base. Then, red litmus differentiates acid from water.

  3. Test with red litmus paper, then use methyl orange on the remaining liquids.
  4. Test with methyl orange, then use red litmus paper on the remaining liquids.

Methyl orange identifies the acid. Then, blue litmus differentiates the base from water.

Red litmus paper identifies the base. Then, bromothymol blue differentiates acid from water.

Question 43easy

What is the pH of a basic solution with a pOH of 3?

  1. 3
  2. 11
  3. 12
  4. 14
Show answer

Answer: 11

pH + pOH = 14, therefore pH = 14 - pOH = 14 - 3 = 11.

Question 44easy

What is the pH of a basic solution with a pOH of 5?

  1. 5
  2. 9
  3. 10
  4. 11
Show answer

Answer: 9

pH + pOH = 14, therefore pH = 14 - pOH = 14 - 5 = 9.

Show answer

Answer: Increases

Question 1336hard

  1. Synthesis
  2. Decomposition
  3. Neutralization
  4. Oxidation
Show answer
